Just viewed this on Paramount+ on their free 7-day trial. I'm glad I didn't pay. Especially a movie ticket price. I'm not saying this movie is bad. This is okay for a fanfiction story, actually semi-decent quality fanfiction, but my problem is and I knew it would be---it absolutely felt like fanfiction. Some fanfictions are so fantastic that they don't feel like they were written by a fan but that they could be a new creation by the original creator. Those are extremely rare and this is not one of those. But then, it seemed like it didn't want to be either. I guess this works and achieved very well for what it wanted to be. This movie had its moments, and I kinda see what Kevin Williamson meant when he said that the writers understood the heart of the Scream movies, but...That's not enough for me if it still feels like fanfiction. This may sound like I went in wanting to not like this, but that's not the case. Which is why I don't hate this and don't think this was waste of time. I'm simply glad I didn't pay to see this, am unlikely to watch this again, and this didn't exactly leave a lasting impression.  In my opinion the Scream movies deserved more than self-aware fanfiction. I don't know why Williamson didn't just write Scream 5 himself if a movie company was interested in funding another one. He has said 5 and 6 are all in his mind as in he has/had a vision for how his original story would have continued. That's what I'd want to see, that's what I'd support by paying to see. I tell you, one thing I'm glad about though, is that this movie made zero direct references to Scream 3. As in, I don't think everything Williamson has thought up is gold. Still it's his vision that started this and I feel it's his vision that should end it when it comes to Sidney's story.   I'm not saying fanfiction is inferior form of writing, no. I don't think that. Even less than great fanfiction can be enjoyable and is worthy of analysing, feedback and such and at best it can be a heart-felt love-letter and tribute to the original. Just...I don't think it shoudl be inserted into franchises on this high level. At least not as long as the original creator is still with us and able to continue the story themselves. Until the original creator is gone, fanfiction ought to stay in the internet and in self-published books. The torch should not be passed in this way too soon.

The stu being the killer idea is a mixed bag for me.  I've been commenting on lots of videos about this.  But part of the appeal of Scream is that it is based in the real world and is conceivably possible, and that anyone can be ghostface.  As the movie series is famous for, there are rules.  And two of them follow in the continuity of the films  1) The Killer(s) in each movie die in the film that they are  in. 2) No Killer has ever come back and resurfaced later in the series, other than being mentioned by surviving characters.  Stu breaks both of these rules.  And it's okay to break the rules, but there needs to be very logical explanations for these things since once again, these movies are supposed to be grounded in realism.  This isn't like the other franchises that have loopholes and oftentimes silly explanations and supernatural shit going on.  These are all human beings that don't have super powers or reincarnation techniques at their disposal.  To me Stu is dead.  And his character holds a special place in the pantheon.  I love Stu, we all do.  But explaining how he got away and survived in the first film is too much, or that he's operating from Prison, it feels way too convenient.  I think the killer(s) will have a connection to the past, we just don't know exactly what that is yet.  I want to be surprised by it.

As I get older and more experienced in writing and producing music and as I study the human mind, I am no longer terrified by horror movies, I am terrified of something far deeper.  And if they made a horror movie of my greatest fear than I wouldn't be surprised.  Imagine we fast forward from 2022 all the way to 2092...  And what we see, isn't what we had expected.  What if the future of flying cars, electronics, and beyond, wasn't coming.  What if instead, human spoils, lead to a narcissistic and strange world of people without feelings...  What if instead of zombies and the zombie appocolypse.  We had a world of psychos, and a psycho appocolypse.  What if, without noticing, over decades and decades and decades of social influence and exposure to violence and grousom events, leads to a sick world that hyper justifies everything.  I'm thinking worse than the purge.  A world rotten, rotten to the core, where the zombies are capable of rational thought yet, normal just isn't quite what it used to be.  This horror movie would be called, MK Ultra.  And it will show you a world where humans become so Godless and so messed up, that death would be more preferable over living in this world.  I see sick people demanding more...  More violence, more insanity, more...  So what line do we cross when it's no longer just a movie behind a screen.

i have to be honest i really wasnt looking forward to this movie when i first watched the trailer but after watching the original again and thinking about it more, i think i see what theyre going for with this entry. Its still a meta commentary on horror movies (specifically halloween 2018), but its much more hidden this time around. I can see a lot of references to newer horror movies in terms of the visuals and of course the movie hasnt come out yet so who knows what will happen or if the horror references from the original trilogy will be a big factor, but i think theyre going for a more subtle approach to updating the series for a new generation, the biggest example being with the title itself. at first i was mad that this new entry was just called scream but the more i thought about it, the more i realized its probably an intentional reference to halloween 2018, texas chainsaw, all of those new horror movies that have similar or the exact same titles as the movies that theyre sequels to. im still on the fence a bit, but im looking forward to watching it now, im excited to see if any more old faces will return or if this will be the definitive end to the series (likely not tho, in the word of matthew lillard, LETS FACE IT BABY, THESE DAYS  YOU GOTTA HAVE TO HAVE A SEQUEL)

Something i'm noticing about this ghostface right away is the sheer brutality and almost monster movie esq appearance the killer gives off, appearing behind someone like Jason, doing the classic Michael Myers head tilt, the way it shows off its knife like Freddy's Knife glove fingers. I've read some of the comments left by people saying they like the serious tone, and I just couldn't disagree more. Scream was special because of it's tongue in cheek approach to the slasher genre. It's clear satire and self awareness made it feel fresh and new. This trailer looked so generic, and the main characters- besides Sidney- look so old I can't imagine them lasting two seconds with a serial killer. Dewey looks like he'll die just by getting up off the sofa.  Obviously this isn't the actors fault, but I can't help but find it distracting. I'm not saying the movie is definitely gonna be bad or anything, I'm just really hoping they don't actually try to take it so seriously. That would show a total lack of understanding of what made the original innovative.

Scream 5? "Who'd want to do that? Sequels suck."  Thank you, Randy Meeks rules.  For me, the franchise died with Randy. Scream 3 was ok since it was already planned as a trilogy after the first two. But, yeah, for me there shouldn't have been more after that. Unless, they're gonna pull a Halloween do over and exclude the events from the previous sequels. I mean, this isn't called "Scream 5" so it makes me think it could be possible.  Even still though, even though Randy was one of my favorite characters (along with Dewey and Sidney), I just felt like the series should've stopped at 3. I didn't like 4 and while this trailer is good, it makes me lose more interest. Idk why some of these horror movies have to keep things going. Even if these newer sequels do turn out to be do overs and replacing their original sequels.  Whatever, the other thing this, Randy's death was supposed to show that nobody was safe, not even the beloved characters, which did make sense. But 3 and 4 kept Sid, Dewey, and Gale alive. So, by the looks of it, Dewey could die in this one. Personally, I don't want him to, but the whole point of giving Randy's character a shocking death scene in S2 was to prove that anything can happen to anyone. So this time, one of them better go. As much as I don't want them to. Cause that's the whole point of this franchise: anyone can be a target. And.. "Everybody is a suspect!"

Why the fuck would you release a horror movie in January?
Hey, another Remix movie. Doesn't look too horrible. BTW a Remix movie is like a reboot but it's taking an original movie/franchise with the same elements that made it popular but adding slightly different elements. Also often a Remix movie is self aware to a various degree. Imagine if Beethoven could come back & put out Fur Elise 2 that was the same song but with a EDM beat on top as a remix of the original. Other movies in recent years are Jay & Silent Bob:reboot, Coming 2 America, Ghostbusters21, Matrix 4, Independence Day 2 and a few others. You can tell it's a Remix movie by when they use a lot of the same scene shots or visual styles, same writing & so forth. Also the main characters of the original movie or franchise are not the main characters in the Remix movie. It differs from a reboot in the self awareness, also a reboot often picks up a story where the last one left off even if it's years later. If this Scream movie were only about Sidney & gang as the leads then it would be a reboot.

One of the best things about the Scream movies is their ability to keep you guessing.  Every time something happens, anything, it's a clue and you KNOW who the killer is.  You're certain.  Your gut tells you, he's the one, she's the one.  But guess what, you're wrong.  The writers lay out such meticulous "clues" for us to pick up, and then lead us down a totally different path.  For that I LOVE these movies, and I love seeing all the guesses already about who Ghostface is this time.  Guess what, you're probably wrong!  :)
